    "quiver grassmannians are varieties that parametrize subrepresentations of quiver representations .",
    "they first appeared in literature nearly 25 years ago ( cf .",
    "@xcite ) , but the large attention they received in recent years is due to their relevance for cluster algebras as introduced by fomin and zelevinsky in the series of papers @xcite , @xcite , @xcite and @xcite . to explain the relevance of the results of the present paper and its sequel @xcite , we review parts of the developments in the theory of cluster algebras before we describe the result of this paper .",
    "there are many well - written introductions to cluster algebras , e.g.  see @xcite , @xcite or @xcite . to simplify matters ,",
    "we restrict ourselves in this exposition to cluster algebras @xmath8 that have trivial coefficients and come from a quiver @xmath0 with @xmath9 vertices .",
    "the cluster algebra @xmath8 of @xmath0 is defined as a subring of the field @xmath10 of rational functions that is generated by the so - called _",
    "cluster variables_. the cluster variable are obtained from @xmath11 by an iterative procedure of so - called _ mutations _ , which are prescribed but the quiver @xmath0 and its mutations .    though it turns out , a posteriori , that some well - understood cluster algebras bear simple descriptions in terms of generators and relations ( @xcite ) , the recursive definition in terms of mutations makes it , in general , a difficult problem to find such descriptions .",
    "much work from the past ten years has been devoted to find bases and relations for approachable classes of cluster algebras .",
    "similar to the sharp distinction between the representation theory of tame and wild quivers , cluster algebras are divided into mutation finite and mutation infinite algebras .",
    "while there is little known for mutation infinite cluster algebras , many results have been established for mutation finite cluster algebras .",
    "to wit , all cluster algebras coming from tame quivers are mutation finite , and we divide them into types @xmath12 , @xmath13 and @xmath14 , according to the type of the tame quiver .",
    "the only wild quivers leading to mutation finite cluster algebras are the generalized kronecker quivers @xmath15 for @xmath16 and five other quivers with oriented cycles ( @xcite , @xcite , @xcite ) .",
    "there have been two major approaches to study mutation finite cluster algebras .",
    "one of them applies to mutation finite cluster algebras of types @xmath12 and @xmath13 and makes use of triangulations of marked surfaces ( @xcite , @xcite ) . for type @xmath12 ,",
    "mutations are understood by geometric means , which yields bases for these cluster algebras ( @xcite,@xcite ) .",
    "there are some partial results for type @xmath13 ( @xcite , @xcite ) and a general way to compute euler characteristics in terms of triangulations ( @xcite ) , but this has not been carried out yet for cluster algebras that come from quivers of extended dynkin type @xmath13 .",
    "an alternative approach is due to cluster characters ( @xcite , @xcite , @xcite , @xcite , @xcite ) .",
    "a cluster character associates with each representation @xmath4 of @xmath0 an element @xmath17 of the cluster algebra @xmath8 .",
    "this defines a map from the indecomposable representations of @xmath0 whose image is the set of cluster variables ( @xcite ) .",
    "the cluster variable @xmath17 is given by an explicit expression in the euler characteristics of the quiver grassmannians associated with @xmath4 ( @xcite , @xcite and @xcite ) .",
    "these euler characteristics have been calculated for the indecomposable representations of quivers of ( extended ) dynkin type @xmath12 in @xcite and @xcite and for the kronecker quiver @xmath18 in @xcite and @xcite .",
    "there have been partial results for representations of low rank for other types in @xcite and @xcite .      in this paper and its sequel @xcite , we will work out explicit formulae for the euler characteristics of quiver grassmannians of extended dynkin type @xmath13 , which yields a description of the cluster character for mutation finite cluster algebras of type @xmath13 .",
    "our technique is based on schubert decompositions as introduced in @xcite and @xcite . in the following",
    ", we will explain this approach and our results in more detail .",

    "the technique of the proof of theorem a is to exhibit a particular system of equations for each non - empty schubert cell @xmath35 and solve this system of equations successively in linear terms .",
    "more precisely , the results of @xcite and @xcite provide us with certain polynomials @xmath42 in @xmath43 $ ] . if we denote the vanishing set of these polynomials by @xmath44 , then the various schubert cells @xmath35 result as the intersection of @xmath44 with an appropriate affine subspace of @xmath45 that is defined by equations of the form @xmath46 and @xmath47 .",
    "the difficulty of the proof lies in the intricate combinatorics of the system of equations @xmath42 .",
    "we organize this combinatorial data in terms of the schubert system @xmath48 of @xmath4 w.r.t .",
    "@xmath25 , which is a graph whose vertices are the indices @xmath49 of the polynomials @xmath42 and the indices @xmath50 of the variables @xmath51 and whose edges indicate that @xmath51 appears non - trivially in @xmath42 .",
    "the schubert system comes with additional data that remembers the terms of an equation @xmath42 and their coefficients .    for a given @xmath31",
    ", we can evaluate a part of the variables @xmath51 according to the equations @xmath46 and @xmath47 , which leads us to the @xmath31-state @xmath52 of the schubert system .",
    "certain combinatorial conditions on @xmath52 imply that the schubert cell is empty , and others that the schubert cell is an affine space .",
    "the proof of theorem a consists in a verification of these conditions for all subsets @xmath31 of @xmath25 .",
    "one might wonder if there is no shorter proof of theorem a that uses arguments from representation theory instead of the lengthy combinatorial proof in terms of schubert systems .",
    "we were not able to find such a proof for the cases considered in this paper .",
    "however , the reader will find representation theoretic arguments in the sequel @xcite , which use the results from this paper to complete the proof of theorem a. though in principle , all the methods in the proof of theorem a extend to other types of quiver grassmannians , shorter and more systematic arguments would be of advantage for a generalization of the present results .",

    "in this section we introduce schubert systems , which are the main tool for proving .",
    "let @xmath4 be a representation of a quiver @xmath0 with ordered basis @xmath25 . in a nutshell , the schubert system @xmath184 of @xmath4 w.r.t .",
    "@xmath25 is a graph with certain additional data that keeps track of the defining equations of the schubert cells @xmath35 .",
    "the essential information encoded by the schubert system are the coordinates of a large affine space and the defining equations of a subvariety in this affine space whose intersection with certain affine subspaces yields the various schubert cells @xmath35 of the schubert decomposition @xmath37 .",
    "the defining equations for these intersections can be visualized by certain subgraphs @xmath52 of @xmath48 , called the @xmath31-states of the schubert system .",
    "certain combinatorial conditions on @xmath52 imply that the schubert cell @xmath35 is empty or , in other cases , an affine space .",
    "in the proof of theorem [ thm : the main theorem ] , we will verify one of these conditions for every @xmath31-state @xmath52 of the schubert systems in question .",

    "a _ graph _",
    "is undirected and simple , i.e.  without multiple edges or loops .",
    "therefore , we can identify an edge of a graph with the set @xmath189 of its end vertices .",
    "a vertex @xmath57 is _ adjacent _ to a vertex @xmath56 if @xmath189 is an edge .",
    "link _ is a pair @xmath190 of a vertex @xmath56 and a set @xmath191 of vertices adjacent to @xmath56 .",
    "we call @xmath56 the _ tip _ , an edge @xmath189 with @xmath192 a _ leg _ and @xmath57 a _ base vertex _ of the link",
    ". if @xmath191 is empty , then we call the link _ constant _ , if @xmath191 consists of one element , then we call the link _ linear _ , and if @xmath191 consists of two elements , then we call the link _ quadratic_.    note that our definition of a link deviates from the usual concept of the link at a vertex of a simplicial complex",
    ". this difference could be resolved by adjoining higher - dimensional simplices to the graph such that the links with tip @xmath56 in our sense appear naturally as simplices of the link at @xmath56 . for our purposes",

    "since we will apply this condition also to subgraphs of a @xmath31-state , we will formulate the results in this section for a broader class of graphs with weighted links .",
    "a _ system _ is a bipartite graph @xmath383 whose vertex colours are ` pairs ' @xmath384 and ` triples ' @xmath86 , together with a set @xmath385 of links whose tips are triples and whose base vertices are pairs , and a weight function @xmath386 that associates a weight @xmath201 with each link @xmath202 .",
    "an edge @xmath387 of a system @xmath383 is _ simply linked _ if @xmath388 is a link of @xmath383 and if @xmath387 is not the leg of any other link of @xmath383 .",
    "[ df : solvable beta state ] a _ solution for a system @xmath383 _ is an orientation of the edges of @xmath383 such that    1 .",
    "[ solv1 ] for every triple @xmath86 , there exists precisely one edge @xmath387 that is oriented away from @xmath86 and this edge is simply linked ; 2 .   [ solv2 ] for every pair @xmath384 , there exists at most one edge that is oriented towards @xmath384 ; 3 .",
    "[ solv3 ] @xmath383 is without oriented cycles .",
    "the system @xmath383 is _ solvable _ if it has a solution .",
    "given a solution for @xmath383 , an edge @xmath387 that is oriented towards the pair @xmath384 is simple by ( s1 ) .",
    "we can relax ( s1 ) by allowing several edges oriented away from a given triple @xmath86 , one of them simply linked .",
    "if this orientation satisfies ( s2 ) and ( s3 ) , then inverting the orientation of all edges pointing away from a triple @xmath86 except for one simply linked edge yields a solution for @xmath383 .",

    "section [ subsection : computing beta - states ] .",
    "the basic observation is that one can apply property ( ev ) only if there is a relevant triple @xmath49 with a unique neighbour @xmath50 for which @xmath269 is not yet defined . with the help of lemma [ lemma : properties of extremal edges ] and an inductive argument",
    ", it can be seen that the edge @xmath349 is an extremal edge oriented towards @xmath50 .",
    "we forgo to explain this induction in detail .",
    "given such an edge , @xmath50 is declared @xmath31-trivial at some point of the algorithm ( by step or step ) , only if the triple @xmath49 is also declared @xmath31-trivial ( by step or step , respectively ) .",
    "this shows that we encounter at no time of the algorithm a sink that is a triple .",
    "therefore all sinks of @xmath52 are relevant pairs , which concludes the proof .    with these results at hand",
    ", we can understand the approach of @xcite as follows . under certain conditions on the coefficient quiver",
    ", one can define a function that associates with every relevant triple a relevant pair that is adjacent to this triple , and this functions indicates a way to solve the defining equations of the schubert system successively in linear terms .",
    "it turns out that for the chosen function in @xcite , every edge between a relevant triple and the associated relevant pair is extremal .",
    "the orientation that is given by orientating these extremal edges from the relevant triple to its associated relevant pair , and all other edges towards the relevant triple is an extremal solution for @xmath325 .",
    "therefore proposition [ prop : extremal solutions of the reduced schubert system ] reproduces the main result of @xcite .",

    "the following happens if we calculate the @xmath31-state . in the initial step ,",
    "certain vertices , edges and links are marked as @xmath31-trivial .",
    "we denote the system of all vertices , edges , links that are not marked as @xmath31-trivial by @xmath843 .",
    "we see from the characterization of the second kind contradictory subsets of @xmath25 in section [ subsection : bases for indecomposables of small defect ] that for each path from ( the triple with first coordinate ) @xmath494 to @xmath582 and from @xmath494 to @xmath144 and from @xmath582 to @xmath144 , there must be a vertex on this path that is marked as @xmath31-trivial .",
    "since all edges of @xmath843 are extremal , a path originating from one of the triples @xmath494 , @xmath582 or @xmath144 ends in a pair .",
    "therefore , we can apply step [ step7 ] successively to all triples of such a path and see that all vertices , edges and links of this path are marked as @xmath31-trivial without deriving a contradiction . if we have done this for all paths originating from the triples @xmath494 , @xmath582 and @xmath144as far as these triples are not @xmath31-trivial , we have calculated the @xmath31-state @xmath52 .",
    "we conclude that @xmath52 consists of a disjoint union of extremal paths , which are solvable by corollary [ cor : extremal solution for extremal paths ] .",
    "this concludes the proof of theorem [ thm : the main theorem ] .",

    "we conclude that , up to an automorphism of the underlying dynkin diagram , every preprojective representation of @xmath0 of defect @xmath5 has a basis of the described form , and the coefficient quiver of the theorem indeed determines a preprojective representation of defect @xmath5 .",
    "this finishes the proof of the theorem .",
    "a coefficient quiver for indecomposable representations of defect @xmath91 can be constructed by using reflections at sources to simple projective representations whose support is one of the vertices @xmath968 . since we do not need to know the explicit form of these coefficient quiver , we forgo to give a description .",
    "we refer to section 1.6 of the sequel @xcite of this paper for more information about representations of defect @xmath91 . the reader will , in particular , find information about how to glue together two coefficient quivers of defect @xmath5-representations to yield a coefficient quiver for a defect @xmath91-representation .",
    "the dual representation of a representation @xmath4 with coefficient quiver @xmath41 comes with a dual coefficient quiver @xmath969 , which is obtained from @xmath41 by reversing all arrows .",
    "therefore , coefficient quivers for representations of positive defect are obtained from the coefficient quivers of their duals , which are representations of negative defect .",

    "<S> let @xmath0 be a quiver of extended dynkin type @xmath1 . in this </S>",
    "<S> first of two papers , we show that the quiver grassmannian @xmath2 has a decomposition into affine spaces for every dimension vector @xmath3 and every indecomposable representation @xmath4 of defect @xmath5 and defect @xmath6 , with exception of the non - schurian representations in homogeneous tubes . </S>",
    "<S> we characterize the affine spaces in terms of the combinatorics of a fixed coefficient quiver for @xmath4 . </S>",
    "<S> the method of proof is to exhibit explicit equations for the schubert cells of @xmath2 and to solve this system of equations successively in linear terms . </S>",
    "<S> this leads to an intricate combinatorial problem , for whose solution we develop the theory of schubert systems .    in the sequel @xcite </S>",
    "<S> , we extend the result of this paper to all indecomposable representations @xmath4 of @xmath0 and determine explicit formulae for their @xmath7-polynomials . </S>"
